<p><b>Guangzhou Evergrande Taobao Football Club</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> is a professional <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">Chinese</a> <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> club that participates in the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Super_League" title="Chinese Super League">Chinese Super League</a> under the license of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Football_Association" title="Chinese Football Association">Chinese Football Association</a>. The team is based in <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a>, and their home stadium is the <a href="/wiki/Tianhe_Stadium" title="Tianhe Stadium">Tianhe Stadium</a> which has a seating capacity of 58,500. Their majority shareholders are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evergrande_Real_Estate_Group" title="Evergrande Real Estate Group">Evergrande Real Estate Group</a> (56.71%) and the <a href="/wiki/E-commerce" title="E-commerce">e-commerce</a> company <a href="/wiki/Alibaba_Group" title="Alibaba Group">Alibaba Group</a> (37.81%) as at 30 June 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> In late 2015 shares of the football clubs was started to trade in Chinese OTC system (<a href="/wiki/National_Equities_Exchange_and_Quotations" title="National Equities Exchange and Quotations">NEEQ</a>: <a class="external text" href="http://www.neeq.com.cn/nq/quotation.html?companyCode=834338&amp;tabId=G" rel="nofollow">834338</a>).</p>
<p>They were founded in 1954, and won several second tier titles before they became professional in 1993. Their results improved, leading to a runners-up spot in China's top tier. Unable to improve upon these results the club went through a period of stagnation and decline before they experienced a brief revival when they won the 2007 second division. In 2009 the club were embroiled in a match-fixing scandal and they were punished with relegation. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evergrande_Real_Estate_Group" title="Evergrande Real Estate Group">Evergrande Real Estate Group</a> decided to purchase the club and pumped significant funds into the team. They immediately won promotion and gained their first top tier title in the 2011 season. The club is the only Chinese football club to win <a href="/wiki/AFC_Champions_League" title="AFC Champions League">AFC Champions League</a> twice, in 2013 and 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The club is also the first Chinese club to participate in the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="FIFA Club World Cup">FIFA Club World Cup</a>, making its first appearance in 2013.</p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a>, Guangzhou Evergrande is the most valuable football team in China, with a team value of US$282 million and an estimated revenue of US$57 million in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> However, the actual figures were total assets <a href="/wiki/Renminbi" title="Renminbi">CN¥</a>2.009 <a href="/wiki/1,000,000,000" title="1,000,000,000">billion</a>, net assets CN¥524.9 million, revenue CN¥380.6 million and net loss of CN¥953.2 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou_Evergrande_Taobao_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In June 1954, the local <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a> sports body founded Guangzhou FC to take part in the recently formed Chinese national football league. They entered the club in the 1955 league season and named Luo Dizhi as their first manager. He guided them to an eighth spot finish in their debut campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The league had grown to incorporate a second tier and their debut season performance final standing relegated them to the second division. Guangzhou won the division championship, however the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Football_Association" title="Chinese Football Association">Chinese Football Association</a> decided to restructure the league at the beginning of the 1957 season and Guangzhou were denied promotion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Despite this, Luo Rongman managed the team to win the 1958 second division title; however, the club were unable to gain promotion because this time they went into receivership. They were not re-established until April 1961 and were allowed to take part in the top tier. Back within the top division Guangzhou often struggled within the league and were again relegated to the second tier at the end of the 1963 league season. They remained there until 1966 when the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Revolution" title="Cultural Revolution">Cultural Revolution</a> halted football in China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>When the Chinese football league restarted, Guangzhou took the unusual step of abstaining from the competition and instead on 26 October 1977 brought Luo Rongman to manage in their development of their youth team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The team played within the National Youth League until 1980 when it was decided that they were mature enough to play in the football league pyramid. They started in the recently created third division. The club's youth team development immediately paid off and players such as <a href="/wiki/Mai_Chao" title="Mai Chao">Mai Chao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zhao_Dayu" title="Zhao Dayu">Zhao Dayu</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Wu_Qunli" title="Wu Qunli">Wu Qunli</a> all rapidly rose into Chinese international footballers. Guangzhou gained successive promotions until they reached the top tier. At the end of the 1982 league season Guangzhou were relegated again. They returned to the top division at the end of the 1984 season via the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_FA_Cup" title="Chinese FA Cup">Chinese FA Cup</a>. With this promotion on 1 October 1984, the club was the first Chinese team to gain sponsorship when Guangzhou Pharmaceutical Co., Ltd. signed a $200,000 annual deal with the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Throughout the 1990s, the Chinese Football Association were demanding more professionalism from their football teams. Guangzhou was one of the first fully professional football clubs in China after the Apollo Group took over the club on 8 January 1993. The investment aided the manager <a href="/wiki/Zhou_Suian" title="Zhou Suian">Zhou Suian</a> to help create a competitive squad. <a href="/wiki/Hu_Zhijun" title="Hu Zhijun">Hu Zhijun</a> won the top goalscoring award. Guangzhou were able to gain a runners-up spot at the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Jia-A_League_1994" title="Chinese Jia-A League 1994">1994 league season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The following season Zhou Suian left the team after having twice guided the club to a runners-up position within the league and a runners up spot against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanghai_Shenhua_F.C." title="Shanghai Shenhua F.C.">Shanghai</a> in the 1991 <a href="/wiki/Chinese_FA_Cup" title="Chinese FA Cup">Chinese FA Cup</a>. After his exit, the club were unable to replicate the same results. When influential international footballers <a href="/wiki/Peng_Weiguo" title="Peng Weiguo">Peng Weiguo</a> and Hu Zhijun left the club, the team went into free fall and were relegated at the end of the 1998 league season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> With the management concerned about the team's performance, an investigation was launched which discovered that Wen Junwu and three other players were in collusion with gambling groups and were immediately expelled from the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> In 2001, the Guangzhou Sports Bureau took over the club again. With significant investment coming from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zhejiang_Geely_Holding_Group_Co.,_Ltd" title="Zhejiang Geely Holding Group Co., Ltd">Zhejiang Geely Holding Group Co., Ltd</a> it was hoped that the club could push for promotion. The division was rocked by a <a href="/wiki/2001_China_Jia_B_League_Match_Fixing" title="2001 China Jia B League Match Fixing">match-fixing scandal</a> involving <a href="/wiki/Changchun_Yatai_F.C." title="Changchun Yatai F.C.">Changchun Yatai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chengdu_Tiancheng_F.C." title="Chengdu Tiancheng F.C.">Chengdu Wuniu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jiangsu_Suning_F.C." title="Jiangsu Suning F.C.">Jiangsu Sainty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hangzhou_Greentown_F.C." title="Hangzhou Greentown F.C.">Zhejing Greentown</a>. Guangzhou's new sponsors Geely immediately pulled their funding from the team to distance themselves from the bad publicity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The club went through a tough transitional period until the Sunray Cave Group took over the club in 2004 and started to invest money in hopes of pushing for promotion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> When the <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Pharmaceuticals" title="Guangzhou Pharmaceuticals">Guangzhou Pharmaceuticals</a> group took over the club in 2006, they were able to realize the ambition of gaining promotion. The club won the 2007 division title and entry to the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Super_League" title="Chinese Super League">Chinese Super League</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Guangzhou_Evergrande_-_AFC_Champions_League_2013_(CHAMPION).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="420" data-file-width="640" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Guangzhou_Evergrande_-_AFC_Champions_League_2013_%28CHAMPION%29.png/300px-Guangzhou_Evergrande_-_AFC_Champions_League_2013_%28CHAMPION%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Guangzhou_Evergrande_-_AFC_Champions_League_2013_%28CHAMPION%29.png/450px-Guangzhou_Evergrande_-_AFC_Champions_League_2013_%28CHAMPION%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Guangzhou_Evergrande_-_AFC_Champions_League_2013_%28CHAMPION%29.png/600px-Guangzhou_Evergrande_-_AFC_Champions_League_2013_%28CHAMPION%29.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Guangzhou_Evergrande_-_AFC_Champions_League_2013_(CHAMPION).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The club won its first continental title in 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In February 2010, Guangzhou was relegated back to the China League One in the fallout of a match-fixing scandal despite having achieved a ninth-place finish in the 2009 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The match in question was the 19 August 2006 league game against <a href="/wiki/Hohhot_Black_Horse" title="Hohhot Black Horse">Shanxi Luhu</a>, which Guangzhou won 5–1 when they were still playing in the <a href="/wiki/China_League_One" title="China League One">China League One</a>. It was discovered by the police that the Guangzhou general manager Yang Xu paid ¥200,000 to the opposing general manager Wang Po to secure a win at home and that Guangzhou's vice president's Wu Xiaodong and Xie Bin knew about it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> With the offending participants sentenced to jail for fraud, the club was put up for sale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> On 28 February 2010, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evergrande_Real_Estate_Group" title="Evergrande Real Estate Group">Evergrande Real Estate Group</a> took over the club for a fee of ¥100 million. Xu Jiayin, chairman of Evergrande Real Estate Group, said that they would pump more funds into the transfer market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> His first act was to sign in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/China_PR_national_football_team" title="China PR national football team">Chinese national team</a> striker <a href="/wiki/Gao_Lin" title="Gao Lin">Gao Lin</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanghai_Shenhua" title="Shanghai Shenhua">Shanghai Shenhua</a> for a reported fee of ¥6 million, then he replaced the head coach <a href="/wiki/Peng_Weiguo" title="Peng Weiguo">Peng Weiguo</a> with former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beijing_Guoan" title="Beijing Guoan">Beijing Guoan</a> manager <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lee_Jang-Soo" title="Lee Jang-Soo">Lee Jang-Soo</a> with no indication. In the 2010 summer transfer window, the club signed <a href="/wiki/Sun_Xiang" title="Sun Xiang">Sun Xiang</a>, the first Chinese footballer to play in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> with <a href="/wiki/PSV_Eindhoven" title="PSV Eindhoven">PSV Eindhoven</a>, and Chinese national team captain <a href="/wiki/Zheng_Zhi" title="Zheng Zhi">Zheng Zhi</a> on 28 June 2010. On 30 June 2010, Guangzhou confirmed that they had signed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luiz_Guilherme_da_Concei%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Silva" title="Luiz Guilherme da Conceição Silva">Muriqui</a> on a four-year deal from <a href="/wiki/Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">Campeonato Brasileiro Série A</a> side <a href="/wiki/Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro" title="Clube Atlético Mineiro">Atlético Mineiro</a> with a domestic record fee of ¥23 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> On 30 October 2010, Guangzhou became League One champions for the second time and returned to the Super League after a 3–1 win against <a href="/wiki/Hunan_Billows_F.C." title="Hunan Billows F.C.">Hunan Billows</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 2011 season, Guangzhou Evergrande further strengthened its squad with the purchase of Argentinean <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dario_Conca" title="Dario Conca">Dario Conca</a> and Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Cl%C3%A9o" title="Cléo">Cléo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Although the team was promoted to the Super League in the first year, they clinched the league title in late September 2011 although there were four games yet to play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> In March 2012, Guangzhou played and won their first ever <a href="/wiki/AFC_Champions_League" title="AFC Champions League">AFC Champions League</a> match, thrashing Korean champions <a href="/wiki/Jeonbuk_Hyundai_Motors_FC" title="Jeonbuk Hyundai Motors FC">Jeonbuk Hyundai Motors</a> 5–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> In addition, Paraguayan <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Barrios" title="Lucas Barrios">Lucas Barrios</a> left the German champions <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a> in the summer of 2012 to join Guangzhou Evergrande.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marcello_Lippi" title="Marcello Lippi">Marcello Lippi</a> replaced Lee Jang-Soo as the head coach and brought in South Korean defender <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kim_Young-Gwon" title="Kim Young-Gwon">Kim Young-Gwon</a> and Chinese midfielder <a href="/wiki/Huang_Bowen" title="Huang Bowen">Huang Bowen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Guangzhou was knocked out of the <a href="/wiki/2012_AFC_Champions_League" title="2012 AFC Champions League">2012 AFC Champions League</a> when they lost 5–4 on aggregate to <a href="/wiki/Ittihad_FC" title="Ittihad FC">Al-Ittihad</a> in the quarterfinals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> They were the first Chinese side to reach the quarterfinals since 2006. During the 2012 season, Guangzhou won the league for the second time in a row, becoming the first team in China to win the Super League title twice in a row, while also securing the Chinese FA Cup and Super Cup to become double winners for 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 2013 season, Guangzhou Evergrande strengthened their squad by signing Chinese goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Zeng_Cheng" title="Zeng Cheng">Zeng Cheng</a> and Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Elkeson" title="Elkeson">Elkeson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> This proved to be beneficial to Guangzhou as they became the first team in China to win the Super League three times in a row. The club also won the <a href="/wiki/2013_AFC_Champions_League" title="2013 AFC Champions League">2013 AFC Champions League</a> in the final against <a href="/wiki/FC_Seoul" title="FC Seoul">FC Seoul</a>, after drawing 2–2 in the first leg in Seoul and 1–1 in the second leg in Guangzhou, becoming the first Chinese side to win the tournament on the away goals rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> By winning the AFC Champions League, Guangzhou was assured a place in the <a href="/wiki/2013_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2013 FIFA Club World Cup">2013 FIFA Club World Cup</a>, entering in the quarterfinals, beating the <a href="/wiki/CAF_Champions_League" title="CAF Champions League">African champions</a> <a href="/wiki/Al_Ahly_SC" title="Al Ahly SC">Al Ahly</a> 2–0. In the semifinals, they were defeated by the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">European champions</a> <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a> 3–0. In the third place match, the club lost against <a href="/wiki/Copa_Libertadores" title="Copa Libertadores">South American champions</a> <a href="/wiki/Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro" title="Clube Atlético Mineiro">Atlético Mineiro</a> 3–2 and finished fourth place on the international stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Guangzhou won its fourth and fifth consecutive Chinese Super League titles in <a href="/wiki/2014_Chinese_Super_League" title="2014 Chinese Super League">2014</a> and <a href="/wiki/2015_Chinese_Super_League" title="2015 Chinese Super League">2015</a> respectively. On 21 November 2015, the club won its second continental championship, defeating <a href="/wiki/Al-Ahli_Dubai_F.C." title="Al-Ahli Dubai F.C.">Al Ahli</a> 1–0 on aggregate in the <a href="/wiki/2015_AFC_Champions_League_Final" title="2015 AFC Champions League Final">2015 AFC Champions League Final</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/2015_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2015 FIFA Club World Cup">2015 FIFA Club World Cup</a>, Guangzhou won 2-1 against <a href="/wiki/Club_Am%C3%A9rica" title="Club América">Club América</a> in the quarterfinals before losing 3-0 against <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> in the semifinals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> At the end, Guangzhou lost the third place match 2-1 against <a href="/wiki/Sanfrecce_Hiroshima" title="Sanfrecce Hiroshima">Hiroshima Sanfrecce</a>, ending up in the same position as the 2013 FIFA Club World Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou_Evergrande_Taobao_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>When professionalism was established within the Chinese football leagues in 1994, it opened the door for more than one team within each region. This saw the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Matsunichi_F.C." title="Guangzhou Matsunichi F.C.">Guangzhou Matsunichi</a> which used to be the youth academy of Guangzhou FC but were sold off to Matsunichi Digital Holdings Limited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Direct ties between these two teams also saw them share the <a href="/wiki/Yuexiushan_Stadium" title="Yuexiushan Stadium">Yuexiushan Stadium</a>. In their first meeting in the first round of the 1995 Chinese FA Cup, Matsunichi beat Guangzhou FC 4–3 on aggregate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> For a brief period during the 1998 season, both teams were in the top tier with Matsunichi finishing higher than Guangzhou FC; however, the rivalry would reach its peak and subsequent conclusion during the 2000 season with both clubs in the second tier fighting relegation. On 15 July 2000, Guangzhou FC won 3–1 against Matsunichi which inevitability helped lead to Matsunichi's relegation, causing Matsunichi to disband at the end of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>When <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_R%26F_F.C." title="Guangzhou R&amp;F F.C.">Guangzhou R&amp;F</a> moved to the city of <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a>, a local derby, often referred to as the Canton derby, was born.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The first Canton derby was at Yuexiushan Stadium on 16 March 2012 as Guangzhou Evergrande lost 2–0 against Guangzhou R&amp;F.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Relations between the two club owners remain cordial off the pitch and club owners <a href="/wiki/Xu_Jiayin" title="Xu Jiayin">Xu Jiayin</a> and Zhang Li were seen enjoying a meal together instead of watching the second derby in 2012 which Guangzhou R&amp;F also won.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_records">Club records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou_Evergrande_Taobao_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Club records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><small>Since <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Jia-A_League_1994" title="Chinese Jia-A League 1994">1994</a> the first professional league season. Correct as of 27 November 2016.</small></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Wins">Wins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou_Evergrande_Taobao_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Wins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><b>Record home win:</b> 10–0 against <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Yoyo_F.C." title="Nanjing Yoyo F.C.">Nanjing Yoyo</a> in <a href="/wiki/China_League_One" title="China League One">China League One</a>, 21 July 2010</li>
<li><b>Record away win:</b> 6–0 against <a href="/wiki/Shijiazhuang_Ever_Bright_F.C." title="Shijiazhuang Ever Bright F.C.">Shijiazhuang Ever Bright</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Super_League" title="Chinese Super League">Chinese Super League</a>, 15 October 2016</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Defeats">Defeats</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou_Evergrande_Taobao_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Defeats">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><b>Record home defeat:</b> 2–5 against <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Greenland_Shenhua_F.C." title="Shanghai Greenland Shenhua F.C.">Shanghai Shenhua</a> in Jia-A League, 8 May 1994</li>
<li><b>Record away defeat:</b> 0–6 against <a href="/wiki/Changchun_Yatai_F.C." title="Changchun Yatai F.C.">Changchun Yatai</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Super_League" title="Chinese Super League">Super League</a>, 11 October 2008</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Streaks">Streaks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou_Evergrande_Taobao_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Streaks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><b>Longest unbeaten streak (league):</b> 44 games (32 wins and 12 draws) during the 2010 League One to 2011 Super League seasons</li>
<li><b>Longest home unbeaten run (league):</b> 34 games during 2010 League One season to 2012 Super League season (29 wins and 5 draws)</li>
<li><b>Longest away unbeaten run (league):</b> 23 games (14 wins and 9 draws) during the 2010 League One to 2011 Super League seasons</li>
<li><b>Longest streak without a win (league):</b> 12 games (5 draws and 7 defeats) during the 2002 Jia-B League season</li>
<li><b>Longest streak without a win at home (league):</b> 7 games (4 draws and 3 defeats) during the 1998 Jia-A League season</li>
<li><b>Longest streak without a win away (league):</b> 21 games (11 draws and 10 defeats) during 1996 to 1998 Jia-A League seasons</li>
<li><b>Longest winning streak (league):</b> 9 games during the 2007 League One season, 2014 Super League season and 2016 season</li>
<li><b>Longest home winning streak (league):</b> 12 games during the 2011 to 2012 Super League season</li>
<li><b>Longest away winning streak (league):</b> 10 games during the 2015 Super League season</li>
<li><b>Longest losing streak (league):</b> 6 games during the 1998 Jia-A League season</li>
<li><b>Longest home losing streak (league):</b> 3 games during the 1998 Jia-A League season</li>
<li><b>Longest away losing streak (league):</b> 7 games during 1999 to 2000 Jia-B League seasons</li>
<li><b>Longest drawing streak (league):</b> 6 games during the 2004 League One season</li>
<li><b>Longest home drawing streak (league):</b> 3 games during the 2000 Jia-B League season, 2004 League One season, 2009 Super League season and 2015 Super League season</li>
<li><b>Longest away drawing streak (league):</b> 4 games during 2000 to 2001 Jia-B League seasons</li>
<li><b>Longest scoring run (league):</b> 23 games during the 2010 League One to 2011 Super League season</li>
<li><b>Longest scoring run at home (league):</b> 36 games during 2010 League One to 2012 Super League season</li>
<li><b>Longest scoring run away (league):</b> 11 games during the 2010 League One to 2011 Super League seasons and during 2013 Super League season</li>
<li><b>Longest non-scoring run (league):</b> 6 games during the 1997 Jia-A League season</li>
<li><b>Longest non-scoring run at home (league):</b> 3 games during the 1997 Jia-A League season and 1999 Jia-B League season</li>
<li><b>Longest non-scoring run away (league):</b> 9 games during the 1997 Jia-A League season</li>
<li><b>Longest streak without conceding a goal (league):</b> 4 games during 2001 to 2002 Jia-B League seasons and 2007 League One season</li>
<li><b>Longest streak without conceding a goal at home (league):</b> 7 games during 2001 to 2002 Jia-B League seasons</li>
<li><b>Longest streak without conceding a goal away (league):</b> 4 games during the 2010 League One season and 2011 Super League season</li>
<li><b>Longest streak with conceding goals (league):</b> 9 games during 2001 to 2002 Jia-B League seasons and 2009 Super League season</li>
<li><b>Longest streak with conceding goals at home (league):</b> 9 games during the 2006 League One season</li>
<li><b>Longest streak with conceding goals away (league):</b> 14 games during 1999 to 2000 Jia-B League seasons</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Record_results_in_a_season">Record results in a season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou_Evergrande_Taobao_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Record results in a season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><b>Most wins in a league season:</b> 24 – 2013 Super League seasons</li>
<li><b>Most draws in a league season:</b> 16 – 2004 League One season</li>
<li><b>Most draws in a first-tier league season:</b> 10 – 1997 Jia-A League season, 2008 Super League season and 2009 Super League season</li>
<li><b>Most defeats in a league season:</b> 14 – 1998 Jia-A League season</li>
<li><b>Fewest wins in a league season:</b> 4 – 1998 Jia-A League season and 2002 Jia-B League season</li>
<li><b>Fewest draws in a league season:</b> 3 – 2006 League One season</li>
<li><b>Fewest draws in a first-tier league season:</b> 5 – 1994 Jia-A League season and 2013 Super League season</li>
<li><b>Fewest defeats in a league season:</b> 1 – 2007 League One season, 2010 League One season and 2013 Super League season</li>
<li><b>Fewest defeats in a first-tier league season:</b> 1 – 2013 Super League season, 2015 Super League season</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Goals">Goals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou_Evergrande_Taobao_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Goals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><b>Most league goals scored in a season:</b> 78 – 2013 Super League season</li>
<li><b>Fewest league goals scored in a season:</b> 14 – 1997 Jia-A League season</li>
<li><b>Most league goals conceded in a season:</b> 42 – 2008 Super League season</li>
<li><b>Fewest league goals conceded in a season:</b> 15 – 2007 League One season</li>
<li><b>Fewest first-tier league goals conceded in a season:</b> 18 – 2013 Super League season</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Player_records">Player records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou_Evergrande_Taobao_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Player records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Appearances">Appearances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou_Evergrande_Taobao_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Appearances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><b>Most appearances in the league:</b> <a href="/wiki/Feng_Junyan" title="Feng Junyan">Feng Junyan</a>, 222 games, 2003–14</li>
<li><b>Most appearances in all matches:</b> <a href="/wiki/Gao_Lin" title="Gao Lin">Gao Lin</a>, 260 games, 2010–present</li>
<li><b>Most first-tier league appearances:</b> <a href="/wiki/Gao_Lin" title="Gao Lin">Gao Lin</a>, 162 games, 2011–present</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Goalscorers">Goalscorers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou_Evergrande_Taobao_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Goalscorers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><b>Most goals in all competitions:</b> <a href="/wiki/Gao_Lin" title="Gao Lin">Gao Lin</a>, 88 goals, 2010–present</li>
<li><b>Most goals in first-tier league:</b> <a href="/wiki/Elkeson" title="Elkeson">Elkeson</a>, 59 goals, 2013–15</li>
<li><b>Most goals in a season:</b> 34 goals, <a href="/wiki/Elkeson" title="Elkeson">Elkeson</a> in the 2014 season</li>
<li><b>Most goals in a match:</b> 4 goals, <a href="/wiki/Hu_Zhijun" title="Hu Zhijun">Hu Zhijun</a> against <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Greenland_Shenhua_F.C." title="Shanghai Greenland Shenhua F.C.">Shanghai Shenhua</a>, 14 August 1994 and <a href="/wiki/Muriqui_(footballer)" title="Muriqui (footballer)">Muriqui</a> against <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Yoyo_F.C." title="Nanjing Yoyo F.C.">Nanjing Yoyo</a>, 21 July 2010</li>
<li><b>Fastest goal:</b> <a href="/wiki/Tan_Ende" title="Tan Ende">Tan Ende</a>, 10 seconds, against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yanbian_Changbaishan_F.C." title="Yanbian Changbaishan F.C.">Yanbian Hyundai</a>, 2 June 1996</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Transfers">Transfers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou_Evergrande_Taobao_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Transfers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><b>Record transfer fee paid:</b> signing <a href="/wiki/Jackson_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="Jackson Martínez">Jackson Martínez</a> from <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a> for <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">€</a>42 million, February 2016</li>
<li><b>Record transfer fee received:</b> selling <a href="/wiki/Elkeson" title="Elkeson">Elkeson</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanghai_SIPG_F.C." title="Shanghai SIPG F.C.">Shanghai SIPG</a> for <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">€</a>18 million, January 2016</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Past_and_present_internationals">Past and present internationals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Guangzhou_Evergrande_Taobao_F.C.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Past and present internationals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
